<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:162px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:SouthAmerica1865_ChinchaIslandsWar.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1151" data-file-width="465" decoding="async" height="396" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/SouthAmerica1865_ChinchaIslandsWar.png/160px-SouthAmerica1865_ChinchaIslandsWar.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/SouthAmerica1865_ChinchaIslandsWar.png/240px-SouthAmerica1865_ChinchaIslandsWar.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/SouthAmerica1865_ChinchaIslandsWar.png/320px-SouthAmerica1865_ChinchaIslandsWar.png 2x" width="160"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:SouthAmerica1865_ChinchaIslandsWar.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Territorial disputes in South America in the 19th century</div></div></div>
<p>A struggle for power emerged among the new nations, and several further wars were soon fought thereafter.
</p><p>The first few wars were fought for supremacy in the northern and southern parts of the continent. The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gran_Colombia_%E2%80%93_Peru_War" title="Gran Colombia – Peru War">Gran Colombia – Peru War</a> of the north and the <a href="/wiki/Cisplatine_War" title="Cisplatine War">Cisplatine War</a> (between the <a href="/wiki/Empire_of_Brazil" title="Empire of Brazil">Empire of Brazil</a> and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/United_Provinces_of_the_River_Plate" title="United Provinces of the River Plate">United Provinces of the River Plate</a>) ended in stalemate, although the latter resulted in the independence of <a href="/wiki/Uruguay" title="Uruguay">Uruguay</a> (1828). A few years later, after the break-up of Gran Colombia in 1831, the balance of power shifted in favor of the newly formed <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Peru-Bolivian_Confederation" title="Peru-Bolivian Confederation">Peru-Bolivian Confederation</a> (1836–1839). Nonetheless, this power structure proved temporary and shifted once more as a result of the Northern Peruvian State's victory over the Southern Peruvian State-Bolivia <a href="/wiki/War_of_the_Confederation" title="War of the Confederation">War of the Confederation</a> (1836–1839), and the <a href="/wiki/Argentine_Confederation" title="Argentine Confederation">Argentine Confederation</a>'s defeat in the <a href="/wiki/Uruguayan_Civil_War" title="Uruguayan Civil War">Guerra Grande</a> (1839–1852).
</p><p>Later conflicts between the South American nations continued to define their borders and power status. In the Pacific coast, Chile and Peru continued to exhibit their increasing domination, defeating Spain in the <a href="/wiki/Chincha_Islands_War" title="Chincha Islands War">Chincha Islands War</a>. Finally, after precariously defeating Peru during the <a href="/wiki/War_of_the_Pacific" title="War of the Pacific">War of the Pacific</a> (1879–1883), Chile emerged as the dominant power of the Pacific Coast of South America. In the Atlantic side, <a href="/wiki/Paraguay" title="Paraguay">Paraguay</a> attempted to gain a more dominant status in the region, but an alliance of Argentina, Brazil, and Uruguay (in the resulting 1864–1870 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/War_of_the_Triple_Alliance" title="War of the Triple Alliance">War of the Triple Alliance</a>) ended Paraguayan ambitions. Thereupon, the <a href="/wiki/Southern_Cone" title="Southern Cone">Southern Cone</a> nations of Argentina, Brazil, and Chile entered the 20th century as the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/ABC_nations" title="ABC nations">major continental powers</a>.
</p><p>A few countries did not gain independence until the 20th century:
</p>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Panama" title="Panama">Panama</a>, from <a href="/wiki/Colombia" title="Colombia">Colombia</a>, in 1903</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Trinidad_and_Tobago" title="Trinidad and Tobago">Trinidad and Tobago</a>, from the United Kingdom, in 1962</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Guyana" title="Guyana">Guyana</a>, from the United Kingdom, in 1966</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Suriname" title="Suriname">Suriname</a>, from the <a href="/wiki/Netherlands" title="Netherlands">Netherlands</a>, in 1975</li></ul>
<p><a href="/wiki/French_Guiana" title="French Guiana">French Guiana</a> remains an overseas <a href="/wiki/Departments_of_France" title="Departments of France">department</a> of France.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="20th_century">20th century</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=History_of_South_America&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: 20th century">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:SQM_GE_289A_Boxcab_Quillagua_-_Barriles.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3421" data-file-width="5542" decoding="async" height="154" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4e/SQM_GE_289A_Boxcab_Quillagua_-_Barriles.jpg/250px-SQM_GE_289A_Boxcab_Quillagua_-_Barriles.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4e/SQM_GE_289A_Boxcab_Quillagua_-_Barriles.jpg/375px-SQM_GE_289A_Boxcab_Quillagua_-_Barriles.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4e/SQM_GE_289A_Boxcab_Quillagua_-_Barriles.jpg/500px-SQM_GE_289A_Boxcab_Quillagua_-_Barriles.jpg 2x" width="250"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:SQM_GE_289A_Boxcab_Quillagua_-_Barriles.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/GE_289A_Boxcab" title="GE 289A Boxcab">SQM GE 289A "Boxcabs" 603 and 607</a> hauling empty nitrate hoppers from Tocopilla to Barriles, Chile.</div></div></div>
<h3><span id="1900.E2.80.931920"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="1900–1920">1900–1920</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=History_of_South_America&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: 1900–1920">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>By the start of the century, the United States continued its interventionist attitude, which aimed to directly defend its interests in the region. This was officially articulated in <a href="/wiki/Theodore_Roosevelt" title="Theodore Roosevelt">Theodore Roosevelt</a>'s <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Big_Stick_ideology" title="Big Stick ideology">Big Stick Doctrine</a>, which modified the old <a href="/wiki/Monroe_Doctrine" title="Monroe Doctrine">Monroe Doctrine</a>, which had simply aimed to deter European intervention in the hemisphere.
</p>
<h3><span id="1930.E2.80.931960"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="1930–1960">1930–1960</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=History_of_South_America&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: 1930–1960">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Latin_America_during_World_War_II" title="Latin America during World War II">Latin America during World War II</a></div><p>
The <a href="/wiki/Great_Depression" title="Great Depression">Great Depression</a> posed a challenge to the region. The collapse of the world economy meant that the demand for raw materials drastically declined, undermining many of the economies of South America.</p><div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:242px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Brazilian_battleship_Minas_Geraes_firing_a_broadside.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1332" data-file-width="1857" decoding="async" height="172" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/24/Brazilian_battleship_Minas_Geraes_firing_a_broadside.jpg/240px-Brazilian_battleship_Minas_Geraes_firing_a_broadside.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/24/Brazilian_battleship_Minas_Geraes_firing_a_broadside.jpg/360px-Brazilian_battleship_Minas_Geraes_firing_a_broadside.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/24/Brazilian_battleship_Minas_Geraes_firing_a_broadside.jpg/480px-Brazilian_battleship_Minas_Geraes_firing_a_broadside.jpg 2x" width="240"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Brazilian_battleship_Minas_Geraes_firing_a_broadside.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The Brazilian <a href="/wiki/Minas_Geraes-class_battleship" title="Minas Geraes-class battleship"><i>Minas Geraes</i> class</a> kindled an <a href="/wiki/South_American_dreadnought_race" title="South American dreadnought race">Argentine–Brazilian–Chilean naval arms race</a></div></div></div><p> Intellectuals and government leaders in South America turned their backs on the older economic policies and turned toward <a href="/wiki/Import_substitution_industrialization" title="Import substitution industrialization">import substitution industrialization</a>. The goal was to create self-sufficient economies, which would have their own industrial sectors and large middle classes and which would be immune to the ups and downs of the global economy. Despite the potential threats to United States commercial interests, the <a href="/wiki/Franklin_D._Roosevelt" title="Franklin D. Roosevelt">Roosevelt administration</a> (1933–1945) understood that the United States could not wholly oppose import substitution. Roosevelt implemented a <a href="/wiki/Good_Neighbor_policy" title="Good Neighbor policy">good neighbor policy</a> and allowed the nationalization of some American companies in South America. The <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">Second World War</a> also brought the United States and most Latin American nations together.
</p><p>The history of South America during World War II is important because of the significant economic, political, and military changes that occurred throughout much of the region as a result of the war. In order to better protect the <a href="/wiki/Panama_Canal" title="Panama Canal">Panama Canal</a>, combat <a href="/wiki/Axis_powers" title="Axis powers">Axis</a> influence, and optimize the production of goods for the war effort, the <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a> through <a href="/wiki/Lend-Lease" title="Lend-Lease">Lend-Lease</a> and similar programs greatly expanded its interests in <a href="/wiki/Latin_America" title="Latin America">Latin America</a>, resulting in large-scale modernization and a major economic boost for the countries that participated.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Leonard,_pg._115-119_55-0"><a href="#cite_note-Leonard,_pg._115-119-55">[55]</a></sup>
</p><p>Strategically, <a href="/wiki/Brazil" title="Brazil">Brazil</a> was of great importance because of its having the closest point in the <a href="/wiki/Americas" title="Americas">Americas</a> to <a href="/wiki/Africa" title="Africa">Africa</a> where the Allies were actively engaged in fighting the <a href="/wiki/Nazi_Germany" title="Nazi Germany">Germans</a> and <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Italy" title="Kingdom of Italy">Italians</a>. For the Axis, the <a href="/wiki/Southern_Cone" title="Southern Cone">Southern Cone</a> nations of <a href="/wiki/Argentina" title="Argentina">Argentina</a> and <a href="/wiki/Chile" title="Chile">Chile</a> were where they found most of their South American support, and they utilised it to the fullest by interfering with internal affairs, conducting <a href="/wiki/Espionage" title="Espionage">espionage</a>, and distributing <a href="/wiki/Propaganda" title="Propaganda">propaganda</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Leonard,_pg._115-119_55-1"><a href="#cite_note-Leonard,_pg._115-119-55">[55]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nsa.gov_56-0"><a href="#cite_note-nsa.gov-56">[56]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-navy.mil_57-0"><a href="#cite_note-navy.mil-57">[57]</a></sup>
</p><p>Brazil was the only country to send an <a href="/wiki/Brazilian_Expeditionary_Force" title="Brazilian Expeditionary Force">Expeditionary force</a> to the <a href="/wiki/Military_history_of_Italy_during_World_War_II" title="Military history of Italy during World War II">European theatre</a>; however, several countries had skirmishes with German U-Boats and cruisers in the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_the_Caribbean" title="Battle of the Caribbean">Caribbean</a> and <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_U-boat_campaign_of_World_War_I" title="Atlantic U-boat campaign of World War I">South Atlantic</a>. Mexico sent a <a href="/wiki/Squadron_(aviation)" title="Squadron (aviation)">fighter squadron</a> of 300 volunteers to the Pacific, the <i>Escuadrón 201</i> were known as the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/201st_Fighter_Squadron_(Mexico)" title="201st Fighter Squadron (Mexico)">Aztec Eagles</a> (<i>Aguilas Aztecas</i>).
</p><p>The Brazilian active participation on the battle field in Europe was divined after the <a href="/wiki/Casablanca_Conference" title="Casablanca Conference">Casablanca Conference</a>.  The President of the U.S., <a href="/wiki/Franklin_D._Roosevelt" title="Franklin D. Roosevelt">Franklin D. Roosevelt</a> on his way back from Morocco met the President of Brazil, <a href="/wiki/Get%C3%BAlio_Vargas" title="Getúlio Vargas">Getulio Vargas</a>,  in <a href="/wiki/Natal,_Rio_Grande_do_Norte" title="Natal, Rio Grande do Norte">Natal, Rio Grande do Norte</a>, this meeting is known as the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_Potenji_River_Conference" title="The Potenji River Conference">Potenji River Conference</a>, and defined the creation of the <a href="/wiki/Brazilian_Expeditionary_Force" title="Brazilian Expeditionary Force">Brazilian Expeditionary Force</a>.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Economics">Economics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=History_of_South_America&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Economics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>According to author Thomas M. Leonard, <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a> had a major impact on Latin American economies. Following the December 7, 1941 <a href="/wiki/Empire_of_Japan" title="Empire of Japan">Japanese</a> <a href="/wiki/Attack_on_Pearl_Harbor" title="Attack on Pearl Harbor">attack on Pearl Harbor</a>, most of Latin America either severed relations with the Axis powers or declared war on them. As a result, many nations (including all of <a href="/wiki/Central_America" title="Central America">Central America</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Dominican_Republic" title="Dominican Republic">Dominican Republic</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mexico" title="Mexico">Mexico</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chile" title="Chile">Chile</a>, <a href="/wiki/Peru" title="Peru">Peru</a>, <a href="/wiki/Argentina" title="Argentina">Argentina</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Venezuela" title="Venezuela">Venezuela</a>) suddenly found that they were now dependent on the United States for trade. The United States' high demand for particular products and commodities during the war further distorted trade. For example, the United States wanted all of the platinum produced in <a href="/wiki/Colombia" title="Colombia">Colombia</a>, all the silver of Chile, and all of cotton, gold and copper of Peru. The parties agreed upon set prices, often with a high premium, but the various nations lost their ability to bargain and trade in the open market.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cold_War">Cold War</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=History_of_South_America&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Cold War">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Wars became less frequent in the 20th century, with <a href="/wiki/Chaco_War" title="Chaco War">Bolivia-Paraguay</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ecuadorian%E2%80%93Peruvian_War" title="Ecuadorian–Peruvian War">Peru-Ecuador</a> fighting the last inter-state wars.
Early in the 20th century, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/ABC_nations" title="ABC nations">three wealthiest South American countries</a> engaged in <a href="/wiki/South_American_dreadnought_race" title="South American dreadnought race">a vastly expensive naval arms race</a> which was catalyzed by the introduction of a new warship type, the "<a href="/wiki/Dreadnought" title="Dreadnought">dreadnought</a>". At one point, the Argentine government was spending a fifth of its entire yearly budget for just two dreadnoughts, a price that did not include later in-service costs, which for the Brazilian dreadnoughts was sixty percent of the initial purchase.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58"><a href="#cite_note-58">[58]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59"><a href="#cite_note-59">[59]</a></sup>
</p><p>The continent became a battlefield of the <a href="/wiki/Cold_War" title="Cold War">Cold War</a> in the late 20th century. Some democratically elected governments of Argentina, Brazil, Chile, Uruguay, and Paraguay were overthrown or displaced by military dictatorships in the 1960s and 1970s. To curtail opposition, their governments detained tens of thousands of <a href="/wiki/Political_prisoner" title="Political prisoner">political prisoners</a>, many of whom were tortured and/or killed on <a href="/wiki/Operation_Condor" title="Operation Condor">inter-state collaboration</a>. Economically, they began a transition to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Neoliberal" title="Neoliberal">neoliberal</a> economic policies. They placed their own actions within the US Cold War doctrine of "National Security" against internal subversion. Throughout the 1980s and 1990s, Peru suffered from <a href="/wiki/Internal_conflict_in_Peru" title="Internal conflict in Peru">an internal conflict</a>. South America, like many other continents, became a battlefield for the <a href="/wiki/Superpower" title="Superpower">superpowers</a> during the <a href="/wiki/Cold_War" title="Cold War">Cold War</a> in the late 20th century. In the postwar period, the expansion of <a href="/wiki/Communism" title="Communism">communism</a> became the greatest political issue for both the United States and governments in the region. The start of the <a href="/wiki/Cold_War" title="Cold War">Cold War</a> forced governments to choose between the United States and the <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Union" title="Soviet Union">Soviet Union</a>.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Late_20th_century_military_regimes_and_revolutions">Late 20th century military regimes and revolutions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=History_of_South_America&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Late 20th century military regimes and revolutions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:242px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Presidentes_unasur_(cropped).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1002" data-file-width="2480" decoding="async" height="97" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ca/Presidentes_unasur_%28cropped%29.jpg/240px-Presidentes_unasur_%28cropped%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ca/Presidentes_unasur_%28cropped%29.jpg/360px-Presidentes_unasur_%28cropped%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ca/Presidentes_unasur_%28cropped%29.jpg/480px-Presidentes_unasur_%28cropped%29.jpg 2x" width="240"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Presidentes_unasur_(cropped).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Presidents of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/UNASUR" title="UNASUR">UNASUR</a> member states at the Second Summit on 23 May 2008.</div></div></div>
<p>By the 1970s, leftists had acquired a significant political influence which prompted the right-wing, ecclesiastical authorities and a large portion of each individual country's upper class to support coups d'état to avoid what they perceived as a communist threat. This was further fueled by Cuban and United States intervention which led to a political polarisation. Most South American countries were in some periods ruled by <a href="/wiki/Military_dictatorship" title="Military dictatorship">military dictatorships</a> that were supported by the United States of America.
</p><p>Also around the 1970s, the regimes of the <a href="/wiki/Southern_Cone" title="Southern Cone">Southern Cone</a> collaborated in <a href="/wiki/Operation_Condor" title="Operation Condor">Operation Condor</a> killing many <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Leftist" title="Leftist">leftist</a> dissidents, including some <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Urban_guerrilla" title="Urban guerrilla">urban guerrillas</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-60"><a href="#cite_note-60">[60]</a></sup>
However, by the early 1990s all countries had restored their democracies.
</p><p>Colombia has had an ongoing, though diminished internal conflict, which started in 1964 with the creation of <a href="/wiki/Marxism" title="Marxism">Marxist</a> <a href="/wiki/Guerrilla_warfare" title="Guerrilla warfare">guerrillas</a> (<a href="/wiki/Revolutionary_Armed_Forces_of_Colombia" title="Revolutionary Armed Forces of Colombia">FARC-EP</a>) and then involved several illegal armed groups of leftist-leaning ideology as well as the private armies of powerful drug lords. Many of these are now defunct, and only a small portion of the ELN remains, along with the stronger, though also greatly reduced FARC. These leftist groups smuggle narcotics out of Colombia to fund their operations, while also using kidnapping, bombings, land mines and assassinations as weapons against both elected and non-elected citizens.
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:242px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Chavez_Kirch_Lula141597.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1769" data-file-width="3506" decoding="async" height="121" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5a/Chavez_Kirch_Lula141597.jpg/240px-Chavez_Kirch_Lula141597.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5a/Chavez_Kirch_Lula141597.jpg/360px-Chavez_Kirch_Lula141597.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5a/Chavez_Kirch_Lula141597.jpg/480px-Chavez_Kirch_Lula141597.jpg 2x" width="240"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Chavez_Kirch_Lula141597.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Presidents <a href="/wiki/Hugo_Ch%C3%A1vez" title="Hugo Chávez">Hugo Chávez</a>, <a href="/wiki/N%C3%A9stor_Kirchner" title="Néstor Kirchner">Néstor Kirchner</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Luiz_In%C3%A1cio_Lula_da_Silva" title="Luiz Inácio Lula da Silva">Luiz Inácio Lula da Silva</a> met on January 19, 2006, in <a href="/wiki/Granja_do_Torto" title="Granja do Torto">Granja do Torto</a></div></div></div> <div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:242px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Flag_of_UNASUR.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="900" decoding="async" height="160" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/Flag_of_UNASUR.svg/240px-Flag_of_UNASUR.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/Flag_of_UNASUR.svg/360px-Flag_of_UNASUR.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/Flag_of_UNASUR.svg/480px-Flag_of_UNASUR.svg.png 2x" width="240"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Flag_of_UNASUR.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Flag of the <a href="/wiki/Union_of_South_American_Nations" title="Union of South American Nations">Union of South American Nations</a></div></div></div>
<p>Revolutionary movements and right-wing military dictatorships became common after <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a>, but since the 1980s, a wave of democratisation came through the continent, and democratic rule is widespread now.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61"><a href="#cite_note-61">[61]</a></sup> Nonetheless, allegations of corruption are still very common, and several countries have developed crises which have forced the resignation of their governments, although, in most occasions, regular civilian succession has continued.
</p><p>In the 1960s and 1970s, the governments of Argentina, Brazil, Chile, and Uruguay were overthrown or displaced by U.S.-aligned <a href="/wiki/Military_dictatorship" title="Military dictatorship">military dictatorships</a>. These detained tens of thousands of <a href="/wiki/Political_prisoner" title="Political prisoner">political prisoners</a>, many of whom were tortured and/or killed (on inter-state collaboration, see <a href="/wiki/Operation_Condor" title="Operation Condor">Operation Condor</a>). Economically, they began a transition to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Neoliberal" title="Neoliberal">neoliberal</a> economic policies. They placed their own actions within the U.S. <a href="/wiki/Cold_War" title="Cold War">Cold War</a> doctrine of
"National Security" against internal subversion. Throughout the 1980s and 1990s, <a href="/wiki/Peru" title="Peru">Peru</a> suffered from an <a href="/wiki/Internal_conflict_in_Peru" title="Internal conflict in Peru">internal conflict</a> (see <a href="/wiki/T%C3%BApac_Amaru_Revolutionary_Movement" title="Túpac Amaru Revolutionary Movement">Túpac Amaru Revolutionary Movement</a> and <a href="/wiki/Shining_Path" title="Shining Path">Shining Path</a>). Revolutionary movements and right-wing military dictatorships have been common, but starting in the 1980s a wave of democratization came through the continent, and democratic rule is now widespread. Allegations of corruption remain common, and several nations have seen crises which have forced the resignation of their presidents, although normal civilian succession has continued. <a href="/wiki/Debt_of_developing_countries" title="Debt of developing countries">International indebtedness</a> became a recurrent problem, with examples like the <a href="/wiki/Latin_American_debt_crisis" title="Latin American debt crisis">1980s debt crisis</a>, the mid-1990s <a href="/wiki/Mexican_peso_crisis" title="Mexican peso crisis">Mexican peso crisis</a> and <a href="/wiki/Argentina" title="Argentina">Argentina</a>'s <a href="/wiki/1998%E2%80%932002_Argentine_great_depression" title="1998–2002 Argentine great depression">2001 default</a>.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Washington_Consensus">Washington Consensus</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=History_of_South_America&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Washington Consensus">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Unasul_29.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1772" data-file-width="2480" decoding="async" height="143" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/79/Unasul_29.jpg/200px-Unasul_29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/79/Unasul_29.jpg/300px-Unasul_29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/79/Unasul_29.jpg/400px-Unasul_29.jpg 2x" width="200"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Unasul_29.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Left-leaning leaders of Bolivia, Brazil and Chile at the <a href="/wiki/Union_of_South_American_Nations" title="Union of South American Nations">Union of South American Nations</a> summit in 2008</div></div></div>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Washington_Consensus" title="Washington Consensus">Washington Consensus</a></div>
<p>The set of  specific economic policy prescriptions that were considered the "standard" reform package were promoted for crisis-wracked developing countries by Washington, DC-based institutions such as the <a href="/wiki/International_Monetary_Fund" title="International Monetary Fund">International Monetary Fund</a> (IMF), <a href="/wiki/World_Bank" title="World Bank">World Bank</a>, and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/US_Treasury_Department" title="US Treasury Department">US Treasury Department</a> during the 1980s and '90s.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="21st_century">21st century</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=History_of_South_America&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: 21st century">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="A_turn_to_the_left">A turn to the left</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=History_of_South_America&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: A turn to the left">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>According to the BBC, a "common element of the 'pink tide' is a clean break with what was known at the outset of the 1990s as the '<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Washington_consensus" title="Washington consensus">Washington consensus</a>', the mixture of <a href="/wiki/Open_market" title="Open market">open markets</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Privatisation" title="Privatisation">privatisation</a> pushed by the United States".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bbc4_62-0"><a href="#cite_note-bbc4-62">[62]</a></sup> According to <a href="/wiki/Cristina_Fern%C3%A1ndez_de_Kirchner" title="Cristina Fernández de Kirchner">Cristina Fernández de Kirchner</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Pink_tide" title="Pink tide">pink tide</a> president herself, <a href="/wiki/Hugo_Ch%C3%A1vez" title="Hugo Chávez">Hugo Chávez</a> of Venezuela (inaugurated 1999), <a href="/wiki/Luiz_In%C3%A1cio_Lula_da_Silva" title="Luiz Inácio Lula da Silva">Luiz Inácio Lula da Silva</a> of Brazil (inaugurated 2003) and <a href="/wiki/Evo_Morales" title="Evo Morales">Evo Morales</a> of Bolivia (inaugurated 2006) were "the three musketeers" of the left in South America.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-VICEtideTURN_63-0"><a href="#cite_note-VICEtideTURN-63">[63]</a></sup> By 2005, the <a href="/wiki/BBC" title="BBC">BBC</a> reported that out of 350 million people in South America, three out of four of them lived in countries ruled by "left-leaning <a href="/wiki/President_(government_title)" title="President (government title)">presidents</a>" elected during the preceding six years.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bbc4_62-1"><a href="#cite_note-bbc4-62">[62]</a></sup>
</p><p>Despite the presence of a number of Latin American governments which profess to embrace a leftist ideology, it is difficult to categorize Latin American states "according to dominant political tendencies, like a <a href="/wiki/Red_states_and_blue_states" title="Red states and blue states">red-blue post-electoral map of the United States</a>."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ips_64-0"><a href="#cite_note-ips-64">[64]</a></sup> According to the <a href="/wiki/Institute_for_Policy_Studies" title="Institute for Policy Studies">Institute for Policy Studies</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Liberalism" title="Liberalism">liberal</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Non-profit_organization" title="Non-profit organization">non-profit</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Think-tank" title="Think-tank">think-tank</a> based in Washington, D.C.: "a deeper analysis of elections in Ecuador, Venezuela, Nicaragua, and Mexico indicates that the "pink tide" interpretation—that a diluted trend leftward is sweeping the continent—may be insufficient to understand the complexity of what's really taking place in each country and the region as a whole".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ips_64-1"><a href="#cite_note-ips-64">[64]</a></sup>
</p><p>While this political shift is difficult to quantify, its effects are widely noticed. According to the Institute for Policy Studies, 2006 meetings of the South American Summit of Nations and the Social Forum for the Integration of Peoples demonstrated that certain discussions that "used to take place on the margins of the dominant discourse of <a href="/wiki/Neoliberalism" title="Neoliberalism">neoliberalism</a>, (have) now moved to the centre of <a href="/wiki/Public_sphere" title="Public sphere">public debate</a>."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ips_64-2"><a href="#cite_note-ips-64">[64]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Pink_tide">Pink tide</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=History_of_South_America&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Pink tide">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Banco_del_Sur.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1442" data-file-width="2100" decoding="async" height="172" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/Banco_del_Sur.jpg/250px-Banco_del_Sur.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/Banco_del_Sur.jpg/375px-Banco_del_Sur.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/Banco_del_Sur.jpg/500px-Banco_del_Sur.jpg 2x" width="250"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Banco_del_Sur.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Rafael_Correa" title="Rafael Correa">Rafael Correa</a>, <a href="/wiki/Evo_Morales" title="Evo Morales">Evo Morales</a>, <a href="/wiki/N%C3%A9stor_Kirchner" title="Néstor Kirchner">Néstor Kirchner</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cristina_Fern%C3%A1ndez_de_Kirchner" title="Cristina Fernández de Kirchner">Cristina Fernández de Kirchner</a>, <a href="/wiki/Luiz_In%C3%A1cio_Lula_da_Silva" title="Luiz Inácio Lula da Silva">Luiz Inácio Lula da Silva</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nicanor_Duarte" title="Nicanor Duarte">Nicanor Duarte</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Hugo_Ch%C3%A1vez" title="Hugo Chávez">Hugo Chávez</a> at the signing of the founding charter of the <a href="/wiki/Bank_of_the_South" title="Bank of the South">Bank of the South</a></div></div></div>
<p>The term 'pink tide' (Spanish: <i lang="es">marea rosa</i>, <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_language" title="Portuguese language">Portuguese</a>: <i lang="pt">onda rosa</i>) or 'turn to the Left' (Sp.: <i>vuelta hacia la izquierda</i>, Pt.: <i>Guinada à Esquerda</i>) are phrases which are used in contemporary 21st century <a href="/wiki/Political_science" title="Political science">political analysis</a> in the media and elsewhere to describe the perception that <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Leftism" title="Leftism">leftist</a> ideology in general, and <a href="/wiki/Left-wing_politics" title="Left-wing politics">left-wing politics</a> in particular, were increasingly becoming influential in Latin America.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bbc4_62-2"><a href="#cite_note-bbc4-62">[62]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pitts_65-0"><a href="#cite_note-pitts-65">[65]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-boston_66-0"><a href="#cite_note-boston-66">[66]</a></sup>
</p><p>Since the 2000s or 1990s in some countries, left-wing political parties have risen to power. <a href="/wiki/Hugo_Ch%C3%A1vez" title="Hugo Chávez">Hugo Chávez</a> in Venezuela, <a href="/wiki/Luiz_In%C3%A1cio_Lula_da_Silva" title="Luiz Inácio Lula da Silva">Luiz Inácio Lula da Silva</a> and <a href="/wiki/Dilma_Rousseff" title="Dilma Rousseff">Dilma Rousseff</a> in Brazil, <a href="/wiki/Fernando_Lugo" title="Fernando Lugo">Fernando Lugo</a> in Paraguay, <a href="/wiki/N%C3%A9stor_Kirchner" title="Néstor Kirchner">Néstor</a> and <a href="/wiki/Cristina_Fern%C3%A1ndez_de_Kirchner" title="Cristina Fernández de Kirchner">Cristina Fernández de Kirchner</a> in Argentina, <a href="/wiki/Tabar%C3%A9_V%C3%A1zquez" title="Tabaré Vázquez">Tabaré Vázquez</a> and <a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Mujica" title="José Mujica">José Mujica</a> in Uruguay, the <a href="/wiki/Ricardo_Lagos" title="Ricardo Lagos">Lagos</a> and <a href="/wiki/Michelle_Bachelet" title="Michelle Bachelet">Bachelet</a> governments in Chile, <a href="/wiki/Evo_Morales" title="Evo Morales">Evo Morales</a> in Bolivia, and <a href="/wiki/Rafael_Correa" title="Rafael Correa">Rafael Correa</a> of Ecuador are all part of this wave of left-wing politicians who also often declare themselves socialists, Latin Americanists or <a href="/wiki/Anti-imperialism" title="Anti-imperialism">anti-imperialists</a>.
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:242px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Dilma_Rousseff_-_foto_oficial_2011-01-09.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3500" data-file-width="2333" decoding="async" height="360" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/81/Dilma_Rousseff_-_foto_oficial_2011-01-09.jpg/240px-Dilma_Rousseff_-_foto_oficial_2011-01-09.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/81/Dilma_Rousseff_-_foto_oficial_2011-01-09.jpg/360px-Dilma_Rousseff_-_foto_oficial_2011-01-09.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/81/Dilma_Rousseff_-_foto_oficial_2011-01-09.jpg/480px-Dilma_Rousseff_-_foto_oficial_2011-01-09.jpg 2x" width="240"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Dilma_Rousseff_-_foto_oficial_2011-01-09.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Excellency" title="Excellency">Her Excellency</a> Dilma Rousseff, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_Presidents_of_Brazil" title="List of Presidents of Brazil">36th</a> <a href="/wiki/President_of_Brazil" title="President of Brazil">President of Brazil</a></div></div></div>
<dl><dt>The list of leftist South American presidents is, by date of election, the following</dt>
<dd></dd></dl>

<li>1999: <span class="flagicon"><a href="/wiki/Chile" title="Chile"><img alt="Chile" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="900" decoding="async" height="15" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/78/Flag_of_Chile.svg/23px-Flag_of_Chile.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/78/Flag_of_Chile.svg/35px-Flag_of_Chile.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/78/Flag_of_Chile.svg/45px-Flag_of_Chile.svg.png 2x" width="23"/></a></span> <a href="/wiki/Ricardo_Lagos" title="Ricardo Lagos">Ricardo Lagos</a>, Chile<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68"><a href="#cite_note-68">[68]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Brown_69-0"><a href="#cite_note-Brown-69">[69]</a></sup></li>

<li>2006: <span class="flagicon"><a href="/wiki/Ecuador" title="Ecuador"><img alt="Ecuador" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="960" data-file-width="1440" decoding="async" height="15" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e8/Flag_of_Ecuador.svg/23px-Flag_of_Ecuador.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e8/Flag_of_Ecuador.svg/35px-Flag_of_Ecuador.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e8/Flag_of_Ecuador.svg/45px-Flag_of_Ecuador.svg.png 2x" width="23"/></a></span> <a href="/wiki/Rafael_Correa" title="Rafael Correa">Rafael Correa</a>, Ecuador<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TRN2009Win_95-0"><a href="#cite_note-TRN2009Win-95">[94]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-drug_smuggling_96-0"><a href="#cite_note-drug_smuggling-96">[95]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-OpenDemocracy_97-0"><a href="#cite_note-OpenDemocracy-97">[96]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-98"><a href="#cite_note-98">[97]</a></sup></li>
<li>2007: <span class="flagicon"><a href="/wiki/Argentina" title="Argentina"><img alt="Argentina" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="500" data-file-width="800" decoding="async" height="14" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/Flag_of_Argentina.svg/23px-Flag_of_Argentina.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/Flag_of_Argentina.svg/35px-Flag_of_Argentina.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/Flag_of_Argentina.svg/46px-Flag_of_Argentina.svg.png 2x" width="23"/></a></span> <a href="/wiki/Cristina_Fern%C3%A1ndez_de_Kirchner" title="Cristina Fernández de Kirchner">Cristina Fernández de Kirchner</a>, Argentina<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CFK_back_at_Olivos_presidential_residency_after_CELAC_summit_99-0"><a href="#cite_note-CFK_back_at_Olivos_presidential_residency_after_CELAC_summit-99">[98]</a></sup><sup class="reference" <div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Politics">Politics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=History_of_South_America&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Politics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1097763485" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><table class="box-Update plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Update" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><div class="mbox-image-div"><img alt="Ambox current red Americas.svg" data-file-height="290" data-file-width="360" decoding="async" height="34" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/53/Ambox_current_red_Americas.svg/42px-Ambox_current_red_Americas.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/53/Ambox_current_red_Americas.svg/63px-Ambox_current_red_Americas.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/53/Ambox_current_red_Americas.svg/84px-Ambox_current_red_Americas.svg.png 2x" width="42"/></div></td><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">This section needs to be <b>updated</b>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> Please help update this article to reflect recent events or newly available information.</span> <span class="date-container"><i>(<span class="date">January 2021</span>)</i></span></div></td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>During the first decade of the 21st century, South American governments move to the political left, with leftist leaders being elected in Chile, Uruguay, Brazil, Argentina, Ecuador, Bolivia, Paraguay, Peru, and Venezuela. Most South American countries are making an increasing use of protectionist policies, undermining a greater global integration but helping local development.
</p><p>In 2008, the <a href="/wiki/Union_of_South_American_Nations" title="Union of South American Nations">Union of South American Nations</a> (USAN) was founded, which aimed to merge the two existing customs unions, <a href="/wiki/Mercosur" title="Mercosur">Mercosur</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Andean_Community" title="Andean Community">Andean Community</a>, thus forming the third-largest trade bloc in the world.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-134"><a href="#cite_note-134">[132]</a></sup> The organization is planning for political integration in the <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a> style, seeking to establish free movement of people, economic development, a common defense policy and the elimination of <a href="/wiki/Tariff" title="Tariff">tariffs</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2010)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> According to <a href="/wiki/Noam_Chomsky" title="Noam Chomsky">Noam Chomsky</a>, USAN represents that "for the first time since the European conquest, Latin America began to move towards integration".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-135"><a href="#cite_note-135">[133]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-136"><a href="#cite_note-136">[134]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-137"><a href="#cite_note-137">[135]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-138"><a href="#cite_note-138">[136]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-139"><a href="#cite_note-139">[137]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-140"><a href="#cite_note-140">[138]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-141"><a href="#cite_note-141">[139]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-142"><a href="#cite_note-142">[140]</a></sup>
</p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Most_recent_heads_of_state_in_South_America">Most recent heads of state in South America</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=History_of_South_America&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Most recent heads of state in South America">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>

<li>2021: <span class="flagicon"><a href="/wiki/Ecuador" title="Ecuador"><img alt="Ecuador" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="960" data-file-width="1440" decoding="async" height="15" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e8/Flag_of_Ecuador.svg/23px-Flag_of_Ecuador.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e8/Flag_of_Ecuador.svg/35px-Flag_of_Ecuador.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e8/Flag_of_Ecuador.svg/45px-Flag_of_Ecuador.svg.png 2x" width="23"/></a></span> <a href="/wiki/Guillermo_Lasso" title="Guillermo Lasso">Guillermo Lasso</a>, Ecuador<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-161"><a href="#cite_note-161">[159]</a></sup></li>
<li>2021: <span class="flagicon"><a href="/wiki/Peru" title="Peru"><img alt="Peru" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="900" decoding="async" height="15" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cf/Flag_of_Peru.svg/23px-Flag_of_Peru.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cf/Flag_of_Peru.svg/35px-Flag_of_Peru.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cf/Flag_of_Peru.svg/45px-Flag_of_Peru.svg.png 2x" width="23"/></a></span> <a href="/wiki/Pedro_Castillo" title="Pedro Castillo">Pedro Castillo</a>, Peru<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-DW.COM_131-1"><a href="#cite_note-DW.COM-131">[129]</a></sup></li>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notes">Notes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=History_of_South_America&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Notes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1011085734">.mw-parser-output .reflist{font-size:90%;margin-bottom:0.5em;list-style-type:decimal}.mw-parser-output .reflist .references{font-size:100%;margin-bottom:0;list-style-type:inherit}.mw-parser-output .reflist-columns-2{column-width:30em}.mw-parser-output .reflist-columns-3{column-width:25em}.mw-parser-output .reflist-columns{margin-top:0.3em}.mw-parser-output .reflist-columns ol{margin-top:0}.mw-parser-output .reflist-columns li{page-break-inside:avoid;break-inside:avoid-column}.mw-parser-output .reflist-upper-alpha{list-style-type:upper-alpha}.mw-parser-output .reflist-upper-roman{list-style-type:upper-roman}.mw-parser-output .reflist-lower-alpha{list-style-type:lower-alpha}.mw-parser-output .reflist-lower-greek{list-style-type:lower-greek}.mw-parser-output .reflist-lower-roman{list-style-type:lower-roman}</style><div class="reflist reflist-lower-alpha">
<div class="mw-references-wrap"><ol class="references">
<li id="cite_note-91"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-91">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Morales is described as the first indigenous president of Bolivia in academic studies of his presidency, such as those of <a href="/wiki/Betilde_Mu%C3%B1oz-Pogossian" title="Betilde Muñoz-Pogossian">Muñoz-Pogossian</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMuñoz-Pogossian2008180_83-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMuñoz-Pogossian2008180-83">[83]</a></sup> Webber,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWebber20111_84-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWebber20111-84">[84]</a></sup> Philip and Panizza,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPhilipPanizza201157_85-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPhilipPanizza201157-85">[85]</a></sup> and Farthing and Kohl,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFarthingKohl20141_86-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFarthingKohl20141-86">[86]</a></sup> as well as in press reports, such as those of <a href="/wiki/BBC_News" title="BBC News">BBC News</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BBC_bio_87-0"><a href="#cite_note-BBC_bio-87">[87]</a></sup> However, there have been challenges to this claim by critics who have asserted that Morales probably has some European ancestry, and thus on genetic grounds is technically <i><a href="/wiki/Mestizo" title="Mestizo">mestizo</a></i> rather than solely indigenous.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHarten20117_88-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarten20117-88">[88]</a></sup> Harten asserted that this argument was "misguided[,] wrong[... and] above all irrelevant" because regardless of his genetic makeup, the majority of Bolivians perceive Morales as being the first indigenous president.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHarten20117_88-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarten20117-88">[88]</a></sup> In Bolivian society, indigeneity is a fluid concept rooted in cultural identity;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHarten20117_88-2"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarten20117-88">[88]</a></sup> for instance, many indigenous individuals that have settled in urban areas and abandoned their traditional rural customs have come to identify as <i>mestizo</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFarthingKohl201422_89-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFarthingKohl201422-89">[89]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESivak201082–83Harten2011112–118FarthingKohl201411_90-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESivak201082–83Harten2011112–118FarthingKohl201411-90">[90]</a></sup> </span>
</li>
</ol></div></div>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1011085734" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="reflist">
<div class="mw-references-wrap"><ol class="references">
<li id="cite_note-103"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-103">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">She is variously known as Cristina Fernández,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CFK_to_Harvard_students:_there_is_no_‘dollar_clamp’;_don’t_repeat_monochord_questions_100-1"><a href="#cite_note-CFK_to_Harvard_students:_there_is_no_‘dollar_clamp’;_don’t_repeat_monochord_questions-100">[99]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Profile:_Cristina_Fernandez_de_Kirchner_101-0"><a href="#cite_note-Profile:_Cristina_Fernandez_de_Kirchner-101">[100]</a></sup>
 Cristina K, or Cristina.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Profile:_Cristina_Fernandez_de_Kirchner_101-1"><a href="#cite_note-Profile:_Cristina_Fernandez_de_Kirchner-101">[100]</a></sup>
<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Aerolineas_takeover_shadows_Cristina_K_visit_to_Spain_102-0"><a href="#cite_note-Aerolineas_takeover_shadows_Cristina_K_visit_to_Spain-102">[101]</a></sup></span>
</li>
</ol></div></div>

<li id="cite_note-36"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-36">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">The influence of human alteration has been generally underestimated, reports Darna L. Dufour: "Much of what has been considered natural forest in Amazonia is probably the result of hundreds of years of human use and management." "Use of Tropical Rainforests by Native Amazonians", <i>BioScience</i> 40, no. 9 (October 1990):658. For an example of how such peoples integrated planting into their nomadic lifestyles, see Rival, Laura, 1993. "The Growth of Family Trees: Understanding Huaorani Perceptions of the Forest", <i>Man</i> 28(4):635–652.</span>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Prehistory_2">Prehistory</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=History_of_South_America&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: Prehistory">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul><li><style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1106273507">.mw-parser-output .citation{word-wrap:break-word}.mw-parser-output .citation:target{background-color:rgba(0,127,255,0.133)}.mw-parser-output .cslsa-pub-no-auth,.mw-parser-output .cslsa-authors{font-variant:normal}.mw-parser-output .cslsa-error{color:red}</style><cite class="citation cslsa" id="CITEREFMarshall1988"><span class="cslsa-authors">Marshall, Larry G.</span>. 1988. <a class="external text" href="https://web.archive.org/web/20160827091213/http://ckwri.tamuk.edu/fileadmin/user_upload/PHOTOS/Deer-Research_Program/Class_files/Land_mammals_and_the_Great_American_Interchange_AmSci_Marshall.pdf" rel="nofollow">Land Mammals and the Great American Interchange</a>. <i>American Scientist</i> 76. 380–388.</cite></li></ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Muisca_2">Muisca</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=History_of_South_America&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: Muisca">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul><li><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1106273507" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><cite class="citation cslsa" id="CITEREFDaza2013"><span class="cslsa-authors">Daza, Blanca Ysabel</span>. 2013. <i>Historia del proceso de mestizaje alimentario entre Colombia y España – History of the integration process of foods between Colombia and Spain (PhD)</i>, 1–494. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Universitat_de_Barcelona" title="Universitat de Barcelona">Universitat de Barcelona</a>.</cite></li>
<li><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1106273507" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><cite class="citation cslsa" id="CITEREFFrancis1993"><span class="cslsa-authors">Francis, John Michael</span>. 1993. <i>"Muchas hipas, no minas" The Muiscas, a merchant society: Spanish misconceptions and demographic change (M.A.)</i>, 1–118. <a href="/wiki/University_of_Alberta" title="University of Alberta">University of Alberta</a>.</cite></li>
<li><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1106273507" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><cite class="citation cslsa" id="CITEREFGamboa_Mendoza2016"><span class="cslsa-authors">Gamboa Mendoza, Jorge</span>. 2016. <i><a class="external text" href="https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=NAJ-EM5h4N0" rel="nofollow">Los muiscas, grupos indígenas del Nuevo Reino de Granada. Una nueva propuesta sobre su organizacíon socio-política y su evolucíon en el siglo XVI – The Muisca, indigenous groups of the New Kingdom of Granada. A new proposal on their social-political organization and their evolution in the 16th century</a></i>. <a href="/wiki/Gold_Museum,_Bogot%C3%A1" title="Gold Museum, Bogotá">Museo del Oro</a>.</cite></li>
<li><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1106273507" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><cite class="citation cslsa" id="CITEREFGarcía2012"><span class="cslsa-authors">García, Jorge Luis</span>. 2012. <i><a class="external text" href="https://web.archive.org/web/20140503090004/http://www.caracol.org/include/files/chase/GarciaMA.pdf" rel="nofollow">The Foods and crops of the Muisca: a dietary reconstruction of the intermediate chiefdoms of Bogotá (Bacatá) and Tunja (Hunza), Colombia (M.A.)</a></i>, 1–201. <a href="/wiki/University_of_Central_Florida" title="University of Central Florida">University of Central Florida</a>.</cite></li>
<li><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1106273507" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><cite class="citation cslsa" id="CITEREFGroot_de_Mahecha2014_(2008)"><span class="cslsa-authors">Groot de Mahecha, Ana María</span>. 2014 (2008). <i>Sal y poder en el altiplano de Bogotá, 1537–1640</i>, 1–174. <a href="/wiki/National_University_of_Colombia" title="National University of Colombia">Universidad Nacional de Colombia</a>.</cite></li>
<li><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1106273507" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><cite class="citation cslsa" id="CITEREFKruschek2003"><span class="cslsa-authors">Kruschek, Michael H.</span>. 2003. <i><a class="external text" href="http://d-scholarship.pitt.edu/7735/1/kruschek2003.pdf" rel="nofollow">The evolution of the Bogotá chiefdom: A household view (PhD)</a></i>, 1–271. University of Pittsburgh.</cite></li>
<li><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1106273507" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><cite class="citation cslsa" id="CITEREF[[Javier_Ocampo_López|Ocampo_López]]2007"><span class="cslsa-authors"><a href="/wiki/Javier_Ocampo_L%C3%B3pez" title="Javier Ocampo López">Ocampo López</a>, Javier</span>. 2007. <i>Grandes culturas indígenas de América – Great indigenous cultures of the Americas</i>, 1–238. Plaza &amp; Janes Editores Colombia S.A..</cite></li></ul>
